Jamison Brereton

34 (225)
Maruts
Gr╠еtsamada
15 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 15
Following immediately on a hymn dedicated to the MarutsтАЩ father Rudra, this hymn describes the Maruts, with the extravagant and imaginative phraseology typically used of them, as the thunderstorm, while urging them to come to the singerтАЩs sac rifice. About midway through the hymn (starting in vss. 6тАУ7), the focus shifts to the benefits the Maruts can provide the singer, in inspiring his hymn, protecting him against enemies, and offering gifts. The naturalistic description remains, however; note, for example, the sequential imagery in verse 13, which proceeds from thunder, through lightning and rain, to the post-storm clearing and rainbow.
The hymn also contains a reference (vs. 2) to the enigmatic and sometimes para doxical parentage and birth of the Maruts from Pr╠е┼Ыni and Rudra. The motif of the cow, especially the milk-cow with her swollen udder, runs through the hymn (e.g., vss. 1, 2, 5, 6, 8, 10, 12), with reference sequentially or simultaneously to dawns, clouds, the sacrificerтАЩs soma-pressings, and the MarutsтАЩ gift to him. This multivalent image helps to unify the hymn as it moves from naturalistic description to ritual entreaty.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Maruts A very difficult hymn, whose problems were perhaps not sufficiently signalled in the published introduction.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Maruts, shedders of showers, endowed with resistless might, like formidable lions, reverencing (the world) by their energies, resplendent as fires, laden with water, and blowing about the wandering cloud, give vent to its (collected) rain.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Laden with water: с╣Ыj─лс╣гiс╣Зaс╕е = from f.j─лс╣гa, water; or it may mean, soma that has lost its strength: с╣Ыj─лс╣гa, apagata s─Бraс╕е somaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Wooers of the gushing streams, the Maruts of audacious power, like wild beasts fearsome through their forces, provided with chant,
blazing like fires, possessing the silvery drink, blowing a whirlwindтАФthey unclosed the cows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is somewhat curious that the hymn begins with the expression тАЬI have set loose my eloquence,тАЭ with the augmented aor. asс╣Ыkс╣гi. Such phrases are more usual in the final vss. of hymns, summing up the hymn that has just been produced. Perhaps here the poet means that he has set his eloquence in motion, in preparation for hymn composition. Ian Hollenbaugh suggests itтАЩs a performative тАЬI (have) (hearby) set loose тАжтАЭ kuv├нd ordinarily appears with accented verb. Grassmann allows an unaccented verb only when the particle and the verb are in different p─Бda – but in other passages where kuv├нd and the verb are not in the same p─Бda the verb can nonetheless be accented, e.g., VIII.91.4cd, VIII.103.9, IX.19.5. (In VII.91.1 the verb is accented though it is in a different p─Бda, but it may also be in a relative clause – though see comm. ad loc.) It would be possible to take kuv├нd here as construed only with ─Б┼Ыuh├йm─Б тАЬsurely the Child of the Waters is one impelling swift (horses); he will make (the hymns) well-ornamented.тАЭ But this seems rather artificial. Perhaps karati lost the expected accent because the h├н induced accent of j├│с╣гisat was more syntactically prominent. In any case the unaccented verb vanate in V.3.10 (cited by Grassmann) is also difficult not to construe with the kuv├нd in the previous p─Бda. GrassmannтАЩs rule seems to be variable: in addition to the accented verbs in different clauses cited above, there is at least one example of an unaccented verb in the same clause – V.36.3 kuv├нn n├║ stoс╣гat тАж (pace GrassmannтАЩs accented st├│с╣гan s.v. kuv├нd; he gives correct stoс╣гat s.v. stu). For further on verbal accentuation with kuv├нd see Hettrich, Hypotaxe 151-52.

As Geldner (and Renou) point out, тАШwell-ornamentedтАЩ (sup├й┼Ыas-) of hymns means not only poetically skillful but also receiving adequate recompense from the gods; cf. v─Б╠Бjape┼Ыas- тАШhaving prizes as its ornamentтАЩ in the preceding hymn (II.34.6), esp. in conjunction with v─Бjay├║с╕е тАШseeking prizesтАЩ in our p─Бda a.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first words of each hemistich in this series of vss. echo each other: 1a ├║pem, 1c ap─Б╠Бm, 2a im├бm, 2c ap─Б╠Бm, 3a s├бm, 3c t├бm, 4a t├бm. Since similar openings are found only in scattered vss. later in the hymn (9a ap─Б╠Бm, 11c y├бm, 12c s├бm) I consider the effect deliberate.

Griffith

THE Maruts of resistless might who love the rain, resplendent, terrible like wild beasts in their strength,
Glowing like flames of fire, impetuous in career, blowing the wandering raincloud, have disclosed the kine.

English translation:

тАЬSince, golden-breasted Maruts, the vigorous (Rudra) begot you of the pure wombof Pс╣Ы┼Ыn─л, therefore they, the devourers (of their enemies), are conspicuous (by their ornaments), as the heavens are by the constellations; and, senders of rain, they are brilliant as the cloud-born (lightning).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The pure womb of Pс╣Ы┼Ыn─л: pс╣Ы┼Ыny─Бс╕е ┼Ыukra ┼лdhani = lit. in the pure udder of Pс╣Ы┼Ыn─л, i.e. on the elevated plural ces of the earth in the mountains; or, an allusion to the legend of the earth’s consuming the form of a bridled cow, and Rudra’s begetting the Maruts of her in the shape of a bull

Like the heavens with their stars they appeared with their spangles. They flashed forth like the rains from the storm clouds,
when Rudra was begotten for you as the blazing bullish (semen [=rain?]) in the udder of Pr╠е┼Ыni, o you Maruts with brilliants on your breasts.

ary├бс╕е is morphologically multivalent; I take it as nom. sg. to ary├б-, with most (Grassmann, Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н], Macdonell, Thieme [Fremdling], Lubotsky, Maurer). Doniger seems to follow Renou (тАЬall noble creaturesтАЭ), but I do not understand how she interpr. ary├бс╕е grammatically. It could also be gen. sg. of ar├н- (or nom. pl., though this would not fit syntactically). _________ 03-04 These two vss. are closely knit together verbally. And finally 3d, 4b, 4d (and 5c) all end with forms of ├бp- тАШwaterтАЩ (nom. pl., loc. pl.), contrasting with the p─Бda-initial gen. pl.

ap─Б╠Бm when the god is mentioned (1c, 2c, 3d).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey sprinkle the wide-extended (lands) with water, as (men sprinkle) horses (when heated) in battles; and they rush along with swift (horses) on the skirts of the sounding (cloud); Maruts, golden-helmeted, andof one mind, agitating (the trees), come with your spotted deer to (receive the sacrificial) food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

With swift horses on the skirts: nadasya karс╣Зaisturayanta ─Б┼Ыubhiс╕е = liс╣н, they hasten with quick ears of the sound; horses are implied; the ears signify the middle parts of that which emits sound, i.e. the cloud; golden-helmeted: hiraс╣Зya┼Ыipraс╕е: ┼Ыipra = the nose, or the lower law; here explained as ┼Ыirastr─Бс╣Зa = a head-guard, a helmet

Jamison Brereton

They sprinkle their horses, like steeds at contests. With [=at the impetus of] the тАЬearsтАЭ of the reed(-whip) they speed with the swift ones.
You of the golden lips, Maruts, constantly setting (them [=lips])
aquiverтАФyou drive to fortifying nourishment with your dappled
mares, o you of equal spirit.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My rendering of nad├бsya k├бrс╣Зaiс╕е тАЬwith the тАШearsтАЩ of the reed(-whip)тАЭ follows PischelтАЩs sugg. (Ved. Stud. I.191; see GeldnerтАЩs n. 3bc and Oldenberg) that nad├б- is here тАШreedтАЩ (cf. I.32.8) (beside naс╕Н├б- тАШid.тАЩ) rather than тАШroarerтАЩ and that it refers to a whip or riding crop of some sort. I suggest that the тАЬearsтАЭ would be some part of the whip, perhaps knots on the whiplashes or the like. PischelтАЩs idea has been generally rejected (though Oberlies [Relig. II.247] seems to accept it); see esp. OldenbergтАЩs negative remarks. But the alternative notion, that the Maruts are directing their horses by the ears of a(nother? side?) horse makes no sense to me: how would such direction work? And although Oldenberg explicitly states that the number is not an issue, referring to plural (not dual) ears of a single horse (or even several horses, since pairs of body parts generally are referred to in the dual even when several individuals are in question) seems problematic to me.

In my interpr. the two instr. pls. k├бrс╣Зaiс╕е and ─Б┼Ы├║bhiс╕е are separate. So also Oldenberg, Renou, though they otherwise accept the lead-ear theory. But Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) construe them together (тАЬwith swift earsтАЭ), which in my view makes a puzzling interpr. even more so.

The next question is how to interpr. the intensive part. d├бvidhvataс╕е. Though the stem is usually transitive, Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take it absolutely (тАЬsch├╝ttelndтАЭ), while Renou supplies an obj. seemingly at random (тАЬqui secouez-puissamment (le monde)тАЭ). I extract тАШlipsтАЩ (┼Ы├нpra-) from the cmpd. h├нraс╣Зya┼Ыipra-, since du. ┼Ы├нpre serves as object to just this participle in X.96.9.

The pс╣Ыkс╣г├бm of d should not be severed from pс╣Ыkс╣г├й beginning 4a, though at least in GeldnerтАЩs (/Witzel Got┼НтАЩs) tr. the connection is not signalled (RenouтАЩs rendering does connect them). In general thematic pс╣Ыkс╣г├б- refers to a strengthening substance, esp.

nourishment. The corresponding root noun pс╣Ы╠Бkс╣г- has the same basic sense (see Schindler, Rt Noun, s.v.), but here in the dat. is used infinitively (so also Schindler, as well as the standard tr.). The phrase pс╣Ыkс╣г├бс╣Г y─Бtha may well be a syntagm, judging from the PN pс╣Ыkс╣г├б-y─Бma in I.122.7 (adduced by Oldenberg), and the acc. appears to be a goal, contra GeldnerтАЩs (/Witzel Got┼Н) rendering of pс╣Ыkс╣г├бm as an adverb (тАЬkr├дftigтАЭ).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe prompt-giving Maruts ever confer upon the (offerer of sacrificial) food, as upon a friend, all these (world-supporting) waters; they who have spotted deer for steeds, who are possessed of inexhaustible riches, and who, seated in their chariots, (proceed) amongst the moving (clouds), like horses going straight (to the goal).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like horses going straight: с╣Ыjipy─Бso na = с╣Ыju akuс╣нilam pr─Бpnuvantaс╕е gacchanto a┼Ыv─Б, like horses going by, or arriving at, that which is straight, not crooked

Jamison Brereton

The ones with lively drops have waxed strong, to fortify all the creatures or for alliance (with them) always.
With their dappled horses, with their unreceding generosity, they sit at the chariot-pole like the straight-flying (birds) on the traceries (of the branches?).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The descriptor ├бsmera-, generally taken as a derivative of тИЪsmi тАШsmileтАЩ, is somewhat curious. It may be simply, as Macdonell suggests, that the waters approach their task seriously, not like light-hearted lovers (sim. Doniger). Or (with Maurer) that they are shy. But I somehow think that this hapax is expressing something more particular, though I cannot define it more closely. It may be naturalistic: the circling waters perhaps whirl around without foam, which might be thought of as smiles. Or it may be meant to distinguish these attentive females from other natural phenomena: lightning, especially, is characterized by smiling (see I.168.8) and laughing, and Uс╣гas also smiles. Though the waters do gleam (see 3c), they are different from those bright celestial females, and the point may be to emphasize the two very different environments in which Ap─Бm Nap─Бt finds himself – the watery and the fiery. Note that in 9b Ap─Бm Nap─Бt тАЬclothes himself in the lightning flashтАЭ in 9b, but by then his assimilation to Agni/Fire is almost complete.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first words of each hemistich in this series of vss. echo each other: 1a ├║pem, 1c ap─Б╠Бm, 2a im├бm, 2c ap─Б╠Бm, 3a s├бm, 3c t├бm, 4a t├бm. Since similar openings are found only in scattered vss. later in the hymn (9a ap─Б╠Бm, 11c y├бm, 12c s├бm) I consider the effect deliberate.

Griffith

They have bestowed of Mitra all that live, to feed, they who for evermore cause their swift drops to flow;
Whose steeds are spotted deer, whose riches never fail, like horses in full speed, bound to the pole in work.

Zur Labung netzten alle diese Wesen sie mit Regen str├╢mend stets auch dem befreundeten, Mit Hirschen fahrend, schenkend dauernden Gewinn wie an der Deichsel eilend zu dem Opferwerk.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, who are of one mind, and are armed with shining lances, come with the bright, full-uddered kine, by obstructed paths, to partake of the exhilaration of the (Soma) juice, as swans (fly) to their nests.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Come here) with your enflaming [?] milk-cows with teeming udders [=clouds?], along unbesmirched paths, o you with glinting spearsтАФ
like geese to good pastures come here for the exhilaration of the honey, you Maruts of equal spirit.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The identity of the three female goddesses is unclear. They could be, with S─Бyaс╣Зa., the three who show up in the ─Аpr─л hymns (e.g., II.3.8), Iс╕Н─Б, Sarasvat─л, and Bh─Бrat─л – though even if so, this does not help much, since the role of those goddesses is not well defined. A (possibly) different set of three females associated with Agni is found in II.5.5, but that passage is too obscure to aid interpretation here.

Macdonell (fld. by Doniger and Maurer) suggests that they are the waters of the three worlds, but I am not aware of a тАЬwaters of the three worldsтАЭ trope.

A more acute problem in this vs. is kс╣Ы╠е╠Бt─Б (in sandhi before vowel; Pp kс╣Ы╠Бt─Бс╕е) in c. There is no agreement as to what stem it belongs to or what grammatical form it represents. Some simply refuse (or fail) to tr. it (Geldner, Doniger, Schaeffer 198-99); others give it a contextual meaning (Macdonell тАШbreastsтАЩ, Renou тАШplantesтАЩ, Maurer тАШnursesтАЩ), without attempting etymological justification. Witzel Got┼Н suggest тАШSpinnerinnenтАЩ (female spinners, spinsters in fact) with a derivation from тИЪkс╣Ыt. What makes the word so difficult is the root accent; it would otherwise be easily interpreted as a past participle to тИЪkс╣Ы. The most sensible disc. of the word is OldenbergтАЩs. He sees it a sexual slang, as in the expression kany─Бс╣Г тИЪkс╣Ы, glossing тАЬdie EngjungferteтАЭ (deflowered girl). Certainly in English тАЬto makeтАЭ or тАЬto doтАЭ a girl/woman is a perennial slangy verb for тАЬhave sex with,тАЭ and one can also adduce the expression тАЬto make (s.o.) a woman,тАЭ for тАЬdeflower, have sex with a virgin.тАЭ He justifies the accent retraction from the ppl. kс╣Ыt├б- (or rather fem. kс╣Ыt─Б╠Б-) on the basis of AiG II.1.19-20, where substantivized adjectives retract their accent. This seems the best hypothesis of a generally bad lot, and it would fit the context, in that p─Бda d describes Ap─Бm Nap─Бt sucking the first milk of females whoтАЩve given birth for the first time (if thatтАЩs what p┼лrvas┼л╠Б- means; see Scarlatta 620-21) – which makes sense if the females just lost their virginity in the preceding p─Бda. I therefore take the word as an acc. pl. fem. to a substantivized kс╣Ы╠Бt─Б- from the ppl. to тИЪkс╣Ы.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, who are of one mind, come to the food that is offered at (our) sacrifices, as (you come) to the praises of men; nourish the cow, (the cloud), so that it may be like a mare with a full udder, and render the pious rite productive of abundant food to the worshipper.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Come) here to our sacred formulations, you Maruts of equal spirit; like Nar─Б┼Ыaс╣Гsa [/him who receives menтАЩs praise = Agni?] come to our pressings. Make (them) swell like a mare, a milk-cow in her udder. Make for the singer a visionary thought that has prizes as its ornament.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In p─Бda a the grammatical problem is sv├аr (to be read as a monosyllable, [almost] uniquely in the RV). Grassmann identifies it as an acc., Macdonell (followed implicitly by Doniger and Maurer) as an endingless loc., sim. Renou However, the phraseology, esp.

the accented asy├б (which identifies asy├б as an adjectival demon., not a pronoun) and the placement of ca (├б┼Ыvasy─Б╠Бtra j├бnim─Бsy├б ca sv├ас╕е, invite, indeed almost impose, a genitive interpr. Geldner achieves this by pronouncing sv├аr indeclinable (n. 6a). However, it is possible to see it as an archaic genitive with zero-grade ending *-s, as in Aves.

xuu╔Щ╠Дс╣Зg тЖР *sh2uuen╠п -s, but with the -r of the nom./acc. leveled into the oblique. See Klein DGRV I.96, Witzel Got┼Н.

The identity of the two entities born must also be sorted out. It is possible that the horse is just a horse, since origin in the water is an equine characteristic (see, e.g., I.163.1 adduced by Geldner). But it seems likely that the carefully balanced ├б┼Ыvasya тАж asy├б ca sv├ас╕е refers to two contrasted entities, quite likely the fire (Agni) and the sun (S┼лrya). The obvious way to get that is for the horse to represent fire/Agni and тАЬthis sunтАЭ the sun, but I wonder if there isnтАЩt a clever reversal: the тАЬhorseтАЭ is the sun and тАЬthis sun hereтАЭ is Agni.

In b the addressee of the impv. p─Бhi is not identified, though the default assumption would be Ap─Бm Nap─Бt. It is striking that this is the only instance of the 2nd ps. in this entire hymn.

The тАЬrawтАЭ (─Бm├б-) fortifications are convincingly explained by Geldner as built from unfired brick. They need not (and in my opinion should not) be further interpreted as cloud citadels (so Macdonell, fld. by Maurer and, in part, Doniger).

Specifying that the fortifications be unfired is a cute reversal if Agni is supposed to be in residence there. It is also possible, if Ap─Бm Nap─Бt is at issue, that the reference is to his residence in the waters, would would most definitely be uncooked/unfired. It is also of course difficult in this post-L├йvi-Strauss age not to put his conceptual spin on the term тАЬraw,тАЭ though exactly how this concept would pertain to this passage is unclear: perhaps it refers to a place and a society so far away (par├бс╕е) from ─Аrya civilization that it counts as тАЬrawтАЭ to ─Аrya тАЬcooked.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBestow upon us, Maruts, that (son) who shall enjoy abundance, and who shall be repeating your appropriate praises day by day to (induce) your coming; give food to those who praise you; to him who glorifies you in battles; (grant him) liberality, intelligence, and unimpaired unsurpassable vigour.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Give us, o Maruts, a prizewinner (attached) to a chariot, a sacred formulation that attains its object, conspicuous day after day.
(Give) refreshment to the praisers; to the bard in the (ritual)
enclosures (give) as his gain wisdom and invulnerable might
difficult to surpass.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the slight phonological play – a: #sv├б ─Б╠Бd├бm(e), b: #svadh─Б╠Бm.

Griffith

Give us a steed, O Maruts migbty in the car; prevailing prayer that brings remembrance day by day;
Food to your praisers, to your bard in deeds of might give winning wisdom, power uninjured, unsurpassed.

Geldner

Schenket uns, ihr Marut, den Siegeshelden zu Wagen, erfolgreiches Segenswort, das Tag f├╝r Tag Eindruck macht, Speisesegen den S├дngern, dem Dichter in dem Opferbund Lohn, die Gabe des Geistes, unverletzliche, un├╝berwindbare St├дrke!

Grassmann

O gebt, ihr Marut’s, wie ein Ross am Wagen uns, Gebet das durchdringt, euch erinnernd Tag f├╝r Tag, Den S├дngern Labung, dass der Dichter bei dem Fest erlange Weisheit, unversehrte Siegerkraft.

Elizarenkova

тАЬWhen the golden-breasted munificent Maruts, yoke their horses to their chariots on an auspicious (occasion), they shed in their peculiar (directions) abundant food upon him who offers them oblations, as a cow (gives milk) to her calf.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When the Maruts with brilliants on their breasts yoke their own horses to the chariots for good fortuneтАФthey of good drops [/gifts]тАФ
as a milk-cow in good pastures swells for her young, they (swell) great refreshment for the person who has bestowed oblations.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda c is a variant on an idea expressed several times elsewhere. that the other fires are mere twigs of Agni, the god Fire. Cf., e.g., I.59.1 vay─Б╠Б├нd agne agn├бyas te any├й. It seems significant that тАЬthe othersтАЭ are not identified here as fires but as entities, beings (bh├║van─Бni) – in my view, because the identification of Ap─Бm Nap─Бt with Agni that brings the hymn to its climax is only partially complete here, and the poet is being canny about not directly referring to fire, though at the same time using diagnostic vocabulary and phraseology.

Note the etymological figure #pr├б j─Бyante тАж praj─Б╠Бbhiс╕е#.

Griffith

When the bright-chested Maruts, lavish of their gifts, bind at the time bliss their horses to the cars,
Then, as the milch-cow feeds her calf within the stalls, they pour forth food for all oblation-bringing men.

Geldner

Wenn die Marut mit dem Goldschmuck auf der Brust ihre Rosse an die Wagen schirren, die im Gl├╝ck freigebigen, dann schwellen sie f├╝r den opferspendenden Mann gro├Яe Labung wie die Milchkuh auf der Weide f├╝r ihr Junges.

Grassmann

Wenn reiche Marut’s ihr, die Brust mit Gold geschm├╝ckt, euch schirrt die Rosse an die Wagen uns zu Nutz, Dann l├дsst die Kuh, gleichwie dem Kalbe in dem Stall, dem Mann, der opfert, str├╢men reichen Labetrunk.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, granters of dwellings, protect us from the malignity of the man who cherishes wolf-like enmity against us; encompass him with your burning diseases; ward off the murderous (weapon) of the devourer.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The cheating mortal who set us among wolvesтАФ o Maruts, good ones, protect (us) from his harm;
roll over him with your searing wheel. O Rudras, strike down the
murderous weapon of the one who lacks proper pronouncements.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This is a transition vs. from the watery to the fiery. тАЬThose sloping/aslantтАЭ in b can be the waters flowing downward, but they can also be firewood piled to be kindled (cf. I.95.5, where the same phrase seems to refer to firewood, as I interpret it), and the golden-hued maidens who circle around him can be either waters or flames.

Griffith

Save us, O Maruts, Vasus, from the injurer, the mortal foe who makes us looked upon as wolves.
With chariot all aflame compass him round about: O Rudras, cast away the foeman’s deadly bolt.

Geldner

Wenn uns, ihr Marut, ein b├╢ser Sterblicher unter W├╢lfe fallen lie├Я, ihr Guten, so sch├╝tzet uns vor Schaden - ├╝berfahret den mit gl├╝hendem Rade, schleudert, Rudras├╢hne, eure Waffe nach dem Verw├╝nschten!

Grassmann

Wenn uns, o Marut’s, r├дnkevoll ein Sterblicher verderben will, o Gute, sch├╝tzt vor Schaden uns; Mit heissem Rade rollet ├╝ber ihn dahin, des Feindes Waffe schlagt zu Boden, gl├дnzende.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, your marvellous energy is well known, whereby, seizing the udder of heaven, you milked it (of the rain, destroyed) the reviler of your worshipper, and (came), irresistible sons of Rudra, to Trita for the destruction of enemies.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Seizing the udder of heaven: pс╣Ы┼Ыny─Б yad ┼лdhar api ─Бpayo duhuс╕е: pс╣Ы┼Ыni is identified with the firmament, and the udder is the cloud; changing the person n: your energy is known, by which they milked;

Trita = a с╣Ыс╣гi

Jamison Brereton

This bright course of yours, Maruts, appears ever more brightly, when the close friends have milked the udder of Pr╠е┼Ыni,
or when (they have set) Trita [/the third (heaven)] to scorning (as does) a roarer [=thunder], (set him) to aging (as do) those who age, you
undeceivable sons of Rudra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. strenuously develops the тАЬgoldenтАЭ theme that appeared in 9d – a color more descriptive of the fiery than the watery. An even stronger indication of the transition to Agni proper is the gerund niс╣г├бdy─Б тАШhaving sat downтАЩ: the lexeme n├н тИЪsad is closely associated with AgniтАЩs installation on the ritual ground (see, e.g., the next hymn, II.36.4).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The ends of the d p─Бdas in these vss. are very similar: 10d тАж ├бnnam asmai, 11d тАж ├бnnam asya. In 10d тАЬThe givers of gold give food to himтАЭ implies that his food is gold; 11d further makes clear that the gold(en) food is really gold-colored ghee.

Griffith

Well-known, ye Maruts, is that wondrous course of yours, when they milked Prsni’s udder, close akin to her.
Or when to shame the bard who lauded, Rudra’s Sons, ye O infallible brought Trita to decay.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe invoke you, mighty Maruts, who frequent such sacrifices (as this, to be present) at the offering of the diffusive and desirable (libation); lifting up our ladles, and reciting their praise, we solicit the golden-hued and lofty Maruts for excellent wealth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Who frequent such sacrifices: evay─Бvnaс╕е = from eva, that which is to be gone to, gantavyam, i.e. worship, or a sacrifice, stotram, yaj├▒am v─Б; y─Бvan, who goes to

Jamison Brereton

Those great Maruts, travelling their ways, do we invoke for you at your ritual offering for quick Viс╣гс╣Зu.
With offering spoons extended, creating sacred formulations, we
implore the prominent ones of golden hue for generosity worthy to be proclaimed.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay they, who, the first celebrators of the ten-months’ rite, accomplished this sacrifice, reanimate us at the rising dawn; for as the dawn with purple rays drives away the night, so (do they scatter the darkness) with great, and pure, and mist-dispelling radiance.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The first celebration of the ten-months’ rite: te da┼Ыagv─Бс╕е pratham─Б yaj├▒am ┼лhire: in RV. 2.5.4, da┼Ыagv─Бс╕е = those who originally were priests of the school of aс╣Еgiras, conducting ceremonies that lasted nine or ten days; here, the office is assigned to the Maruts, as the first celebrators of the rite; they are, therefore, identified with the aс╣Еgirasas– aс╣Еgirasas tad r┼лpa bh┼лtv─Б marutaс╕е, who were the first, or prior to the ─Аdityas; the legend: there was a competition for precedence in going to svarga, between the ─Бdityas and the aс╣Еgirasas, and the latter acquired it, by first instrumental tuting sacrifices with fire, ─Бditya┼Ыcaiva iha asann aс╣Еgirasa┼Ыca te agre agnin─Б agnim ayajanta = the ─Бdityas were also here and the aс╣Еgirasas; they (the latter) first worshipped Agni with fire

Jamison Brereton

The Da┼Ыagvas were the first to conduct the sacrifice. Let them rouse us at the brightenings of dawn.
As Dawn with her ruddy (beams) uncloses the nights, (so did
they unclose the cows) with the greatly blazing light flooding
with cows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verb m─Б╠Бrjmi is accented because of its juxtaposition with clause-initial d├нdhiс╣г─Бmi.

Griffith

They, the Dasagvas, first of all brought sacrifice: they at the break of mornings shall inspirit us.
Dawn with her purple beams uncovereth the nights, with great light glowing like a billowy sea of milk.

Geldner

Die Dasagva┬┤s haben zuerst das Opfer ausgef├╝hrt. Die sollen uns bei dem Aufgang der Morgenr├╢te anspornen: Wie die Morgenr├╢te mit ihren r├╢tlichen Farben die N├дchte aufdeckt, so deckten sie die Kuhh├╢hle auf mit dem herrlichen, gl├дnzenden, rinderwogenden Lichte.

Grassmann

Zum Opfer fuhren sie zuerst, je zehn und zehn; sie seien hold uns bei der Morgenr├╢then Schein; Es schliesst die N├дchte Uschas auf mit rothem Licht, im Herrlichkeit mit rinderreichem Strahlenglanz.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey, the Rudras, (equipped) with melodious (lutes), and decorated with purple ornaments, exult in the dwellings of the waters; and scattering the clouds with rappid vigour, they are endowed with delightful and beautiful forms.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

With melodious lutes: te kс╣гoс╣З─лbhiс╕е: kс╣гoс╣З─лbhiс╕е = ┼Ыabda k─Бr─лbhir v─Бс╣З─Бkyair v─лс╣З─Б vi┼Ыeс╣гaiс╕е, with sounding instrumental uments, called vinas, a sort of v─лс╣З─Бs, string instrumental uments

Jamison Brereton

With their cries [=thunder], with their ornaments like (DawnтАЩs) ruddy (beams), the Rudras have grown strong in the seats of truth.
Pissing downward in a steedтАЩs shape, they have assumed their much gleaming, well-bedizened hue.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Oldenberg noted (see also Hoffmann, Injunk., 121 n. 29), the need for a caesura suggests a reading vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б janayat, rather than the augmented ajanayat of the Pp. (In fact, this suggestion is already found in Grassmann) That two pres. indicatives, dhayati and rihanti, follow this proposed injunctive in the same thematic sequence supports interpreting the form contra the Pp, as Hoffmann points out.

The simile any├бsyeva .. tanv─Б╠АтАЬas if with the body of anotherтАЭ is, in my view, another reference to the distinction between but ultimate identification of Ap─Бm Nap─Бt and Agni.

Griffith

The Rudras have rejoiced thern in the gathered bands at seats of worship as in purple ornaments.
They with impetuous vigour sending down the rain have taken to themselves a bright and lovely hue.

рддрд╛рдиреНрдорд░реБрддреЛрдорд╣рд┐рдорд╣рддреН рд╡рд░реВрдердВрд╡рд░рдгреАрдпрдореНрдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдиреНрдзрдирдВ рддрдиреНрдорд░реБрддрдГ рдКрддрдпреЗрд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдЗрдпрд╛рдирдГ рдЗрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдпрд╛рдЪ- рдорд╛рдирд╛рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕реБрдкрд╛рдВрд╕реБрд▓реБрдЧрд┐рддрд┐рдЬрд╕рдГрд╕реБрдГ рдПрдирд╛рдЕрдиреЗрдирдирдорд╕рд╛ рдирдорд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░реЗрдгрд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реЗрдгрд╡рд╛рдЙрдкреЗрддреН рдЙрдкреЗрддреНрдпрдЧреГрдгреАрдорд╕рд┐рд╕реНрддреБ- рдордГ рдШреЗрддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрдкреВрд░рдгрдГ рдПрдиреЗрддреНрдпрддреНрд░рд╕реБрдкрд╛рдВрд╕реБрд▓реБрдЧрд┐рддрд┐рддреГрддреАрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдЖрдЬрд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГ рдирд╢рдмреНрджрдГ рд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЪрдпреЗ рддреНрд░рд┐рддрдЛрд╖рд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдпрд╛рдиреЗ- рддрд╛рдиреН рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╣реЛрддреДрдиреН рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рддреНрдордкреНрд░рдгрд╛рдкрд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╡реГрддреНрддреНрдпрд╛рддреНрдордирд╛рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рдЕрддрдПрд╡рд╣реЛрдордирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрдХрд╛рдиреН рдЕрд╡рд░рд╛рдиреНрдореБрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдпреЗрдЕрднрд┐рд▓рд╖рд┐рддрд╕рд┐рджреНрднреНрдпрд░реНрдердЮреНрдЪрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдирд╛рднрд┐рдЪрдХреНрд░реЗрдгрдЕрд╡рд╕реЗрдЕрд╡рддреБрдВрд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдиреНрддреБрдВ рдЖрд╡рд╡рд░реНрддрддреН рд╕реНрд╡- рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреНрдирд┐рд░реНрдЬрд┐рдЧрдорд┐рд╖реВрдиреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдиреН рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рддреНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдореБрдЦрдорд╛рд╡рд░реНрддрдпреЗрддреН рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдЪрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдЛрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпреЗрдирд╛рдпреБрдзреЗрдирдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдиреН рдЕрд╡рд╕реЗ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГрдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░рд┐рддреБрдорд╛рд╡рд░реНрддрдпрддреН рддрд╛рдиреН рд╕реНрддреБрдордЗрддрд┐рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рд╡рд╡рд░реНрддрджрд┐рддрд┐ рд╡реГрддреЗрд░реНрдгреНрдпрдиреНрддрд╛рд▓реНрд▓реБрдЩрд┐рдЪрдЩрд┐рд░реВ- рдкрдореН рее резрек рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬImploring them for ample wealth, and (having recourse to him) for protection, we glorify them with this praise; like the five chief priests whom Trita detained for the (performance of) the sacrifice, and to protect it with their weapons.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like the five chief priests: trita na y─Бn pa├▒ca hotс╣Ыn abhiс╣гс╣нaye ─Бvavartad avar─Бn cakriya ─Бvase: the allusion is to the practice of mysticism, or yoga; the five hotс╣Ыs or offerers of the Soma, being the five vital airs, whom Trita, as a Yogi, suppressed, and compelled to concentrate themselves in the Cakra, or umbilical region for the attainement of superhuman faculties;

Avar─Бn = homaniс╣гp─Бdak─Бn mukhy─Бn, the chief offerers of the Soma; pa├▒ca hotс╣Ыn adhy─Бtmapr─Бс╣З─Бp─Бn─Бdi pa├▒ca vс╣Ыtty─Бtman─Б vartm─Бn─Бn, ata eva homaniс╣гp─Бdak─Бn mukhy─Бn, abiс╣гс╣нaye abhilaс╣гitasiddhyartham cakriy─Б n─Бbh─лcakreс╣Зa avitum saс╣Еgantum ─Бvavartat; svasm─Бn nirjigamiс╣г┼лn pr─Бс╣З─Бn sv─Бtm─Бbhimukuham ─Бvartayat, he compelled the vital airs, desirous of issuing from himself to turn back into the presence of himself, and to concentrate with the umbilical cakra, for the entire completion of the rite; (those airs being) the chief offerers of the oblation abiding in the spirit, as pr─Бс╣Зa, ap─Бna and the rest, constituting the five ministering priests; a less mystical interpretation turns upon the sense of cakriy─Б, with a spear or lance, с╣Ыс╣гс╣нy─Бkhyena ─Бyudhena

Jamison Brereton

While one [=poet?] is imploring them for a great defense, for help, we hymn them with this reverence right hereтАФ
they whom he [=poet?] will cause to roll down here with their wheel for aid, as Trita [/the third one] (brought here) five Hotars for
dominance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The acc. participial phrases of ab must be construed with p├бri d─лyanti тАЬthey fly around (him)тАЭ in d, even though the same referent is found in the dat. in n├бptre in c. The latter participates in a clever word play – ─Б╠Бpo n├бptre – which of course evokes ap─Б╠Бm n├бp─Бt even though ─Б╠Бpaс╕е is nom. pl. fem. тАШwatersтАЩ and not part of a syntagm with n├бptre. The elision of the first part of his name may be meant: now that he is identified with Agni, he is no longer the child (only) of the waters. But as noted in the published introduction, that the waters bring him ghee brings the watery and the fiery into harmony. Note that the waters as his cloak here (if I am correct in this interpr., see below) answers to the ghee-cloak in 4d. In the watery vs. 4 the presence of ghee was somewhat anomalous; similarly here in a mostly fiery environment the cloak of the waters stands out.

The phrase svay├бm ├бtkaiс╕е is also unclear, and indeed whether it is actually a phrase. Geldner takes it as referring to Ap─Бm Nap─Бt: тАЬund sich selbst mit Gew├дndern (bekleidet).тАЭ He adduces IV.18.5 with svay├бс╣Г ├бtkaс╣Г v├бs─Бna(с╕е), but in fact the difference in case between the acc. there and the instr. here speaks against his interpr.

The simplex root pres. always takes the acc. of the garment, while the causative v─Бs├бya- takes the instr. Moreover, as L├╝ders points out (Varuс╣Зa, 146-47 n. 8), the position of this phrase (far from the masc. acc. sg. in ab, adjacent to the fem. nom. pl.

in d) and the тАЬharsh ellipsisтАЭ required makes this interpr. unlikely. L├╝ders himself in his tr. (146) implies the waters are bringing the ghee with their cloaks, though in the n.

he sees them as тАЬin Schmelzbutter gekleidet.тАЭ Acdg. to Renou the waters fly around him тАЬavec des v├кtements (quтАЩelles se sont donn├йs) elles-m├кmes,тАЭ an expression I donтАЩt entirely understand. Witzel Got┼Н appear to separate svay├бm and ├бtkaiс╕е but, with L├╝ders, Renou, and me, also take the garments as belonging to the waters: тАЬum ihn fliegen die jugendfrischen Wasser von sich selbst mit (ihren) Reisem├дnteln herum.тАЭ The further (and perhaps unjustified) step I take in my tr. is in interpreting svay├бm so closely with ├бtkaiс╕е, with the waters themselves becoming cloaks for him.

In b тАШpathsтАЩ is to be supplied with adhvasm├бbhiс╕е тАШunbesmirchedтАЩ on the basis of II.34.5 adhvasm├бbhiс╕е path├нbhiс╕е in the adjacent hymn, at least by my interpr. The standard tr. (Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н, Renou, also L├╝ders, 146) supply тАШflamesтАЩ instead (though Renou in his n.

suggests that тАЬcheminsтАЭ could be supplied). Where exactly he is located (тАЬhighest footprintтАЭ generally implies high heaven) and which pathways are meant are unclear to me.

Soliciting their high protection for our help, with this our adoration we sing praise to them,
Whom, for assistance, like the five terrestrial priests. Trita hath brought to aid us hither on his car.

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╡рдпрдорднрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдп рдКрддрдп рдЗрдпрд╛рдирд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рддреЛ рди рдпрд╛рдиреН рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╡рд░рд╛рдиреН рд╣реЛрддреДрдиреН рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╡рд░рд╛рдЮреНрдЪрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рд╜рднрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдпреЗрд╜рд╡рд╕ рдЖрд╡рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрддреН рддрд╛рдиреВрддрдпреЗ рдорд╣рд┐ рд╡рд░реВрдердВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдп рд╡реЗрджреЗрдирд╛ рдирдорд╕реЛрдкрдЧреГрдгреАрдорд╕рд┐ реерезрекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рд╣реЗрдорд░реБрддрдГ рдпрдпрд╛рдКрддреНрдпрд╛рд░рдзреНрд░рдорд╛рд░рд╛рдзрдХрдВрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдВрдЕрдВрд╣рдГ рдкрд╛рдкрдВрдЕрддрд┐рдкрд╛рд░рдпрде рдЕрддрд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдордпрде рдпрдпрд╛ рдКрддреНрдпрд╛- рд╡рдиреНрджрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВрд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдиреНрдирд┐рджреЛрдирд┐рдиреНрджрд┐рддреБрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реЛрдГ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН рдореБрдЮреНрдЪрде рдореЛрдЪрдпрде рд╣реЗрдорд░реБрддрдГ рд╡реЛрдпреБрд╖реНрдорджреАрдпрд╛рдпрд╛ рдКрддрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╛рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЪреА рдЕрд╕реНрдорджрднрд┐рдореБрдЦрд╛рднрд╡рддреБ рддрдерд╛рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рд░реНрдпреБрд╖реНрдорджреАрдпрд╛рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рдорддрд┐рдГ рдЕрдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рддреНрдорд┐рдХрд╛рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд░реЗ- рд╡рд╣рдореНрднрд╛рд░рд╡рдЩреНрдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддреАрдзреЗрдиреБрд░рд┐рд╡рд╡рддреНрд╕рдВрд╕реБрд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрдУрдЬрд┐рдЧрд╛рддреБ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ рдПрд╡рдорд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдерд╛рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее резрел реердЙрдкреЗрдорд┐рддрд┐рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдиреНрддреГрддреАрдпрдВрд╕реВрдХреНрддрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рд░реНрддреНрд╕рдорджрдиреНрддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдВрдЕрдкрд╛рдиреНрдирдкрд╛рджреНрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХрдВ рддрдерд╛рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдЙрдкреЗрдордкреЛрдирддреНрдиреАрдп- рдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛрд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ ред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, may that protection wherewith you convey the worshipper beyond sin, wherewith you rescue the reciter of your praise from the scoffer, be present with us; may your benign disposition tend towards us, like a lowing (cow towards her calf).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

That with which you carry the feeble one across difficult straits, with which you free your celebrant from scorn,
that is nearbyтАФthat help of yours, o Maruts. May your benevolence come here like a bellowing (cow).

Griffith

Wherewith ye bear your servant over trouble, and free your worshipper from scoff and scorning.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) рдорд░рдгрдзрд░реНрдорд╛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! (рдпрд╛) рдЬреЛ (рдКрддрд┐рдГ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ (рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рдГ) рдФрд░ рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ (рдУ) рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдгрд╛рдУрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рд╡рдГ) рддреБрдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреА (рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╡) рдордиреЛрд╣рд░ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди (рд╕реБрдЬрд┐рдЧрд╛рддреБ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ рд╡рд╛ (рдпрдпрд╛) рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ (рд░рдзреНрд░рдореН) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдХреА рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐ рдХреЛ (рдЕрддрд┐рдкрд╛рд░рдпрде) рдЕрддреАрд╡ рдкрд╛рд░ рдкрд╣реБрдБрдЪрд╛рдУ рдФрд░ (рдЕрдВрд╣рдГ) рдЕрдкрд░рд╛рдз рдХреЛ рдирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрдд рдХрд░реЛ рд╡рд╛ (рдпрдпрд╛) рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ (рдирд┐рджрдГ) рдирд┐рдиреНрджрд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЛ (рдореБрдЮреНрдЪрде) рдореЛрдЪреЛ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЫреЛреЬреЛ (рд╕рд╛) рд╡рд╣ (рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЪреА) рдШреЛреЬреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рдХреЛрдИ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛ (рд╡рдиреНрджрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдореН) рд╡рдиреНрджрдирд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛ реерезрелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдЕрдзрд░реНрдо рдФрд░ рдирд┐рдиреНрджрд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХрд╛ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ рдФрд░ рдзрд░реНрдо рд╡рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХрд╛ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рд╣реЛ, рдЙрд╕ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛ рдХреЛ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдХрд░реЗрдВ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рд╕рджрд╛ рдирд┐рдиреНрджрд╛ рдХрд╛ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ рдФрд░ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдХрд╛ рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░реЗрдВ реерезрелрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдФрд░ рдкрд╡рди рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рдЬрд╛рдирдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗрее рдпрд╣ рдЪреМрддреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЗрдХреНрдХреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддреЛ рдпреЛрддрд┐рдГ рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рд░реЛ рд╡реЛ рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╡ рд╕реБрдЬрд┐рдЧрд╛рддреБ рдпрдпрд╛ рд░рдзреНрд░рдорддрд┐ рдкрд╛рд░рдпрдерд╛рдВрд╣реЛ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдпрде рдпрдпрд╛ рдирд┐рджреЛ рдореБрдЮреНрдЪрде рд╕рд╛рд╜рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЪреА рд╡рдиреНрджрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддреБ реерезрелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрдпрд╛) рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдпрд╛ (рд░рдзреНрд░рдореН) рд╕рдВрд░рд╛рдзрдирдореН (рдкрд╛рд░рдпрде) (рдЕрддрд┐) (рдЕрдВрд╣рдГ) рдЕрдкрд░рд╛рдзрдореН (рдпрдпрд╛) (рдирд┐рджрдГ) рдирд┐рдиреНрджрдХрд╛рдиреН (рдореБрдЮреНрдЪрде) (рд╡рдиреНрджрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдореН) рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рдХрдореН (рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЪреА) рдпрд╛рд╜рд░реНрд╡рдгреЛрд╜рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирдЮреНрдЪрддрд┐ рд╕рд╛ (рд╕рд╛) (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) (рдпрд╛) (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдКрддрд┐рдГ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ (рдУ) рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдгреЗрд╖реБ (рд╕реБ) (рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╡) рдХрдордиреАрдп рдЗрд╡ (рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рдГ) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛ (рдЬрд┐рдЧрд╛рддреБ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рддреБ реерезрелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпрдпрд╛ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдпрд╛рд╜рдзрд░реНрдордирд┐рдиреНрджрдХрддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреЛ рдзрд░реНрдордкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдирдВ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреНрддрд╛рдВ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рддрддрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреБ рд╕рджрд╛ рдирд┐рдиреНрджрд╛рд╡рд░реНрдЬрдирдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд░рдгрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпреБрд░рд┐рддрд┐ реерезрелрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрд╡рд╛рдпреБрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдореН рее рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореЗрдХрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
